# Testing IPython Notebooks from MarkDown files

```{.python .input  n=6}
>>> print("foo")
>>> l = [i*i for i in range(100)]
```

```{.python .input  n=7}
>>> %matplotlib inline
```

```{.python .input  n=8}
>>> import matplotlib
>>> import numpy as np
>>> import matplotlib.pyplot as pl
```

```{.python .input  n=9}
>>> # make some random data
... a = np.random.rand(10,5)
```

```{.python .input  n=10}
>>> # Try this one simple command to make heat maps.  Fools hate it
... pl.pcolor(a)
```

```{.python .input  n=70}
### tun1 = data[data['TUNPosition']==1]
C = tun1['VehicleNumber'].value_counts() / data['VehicleNumber'].value_counts()
C.plot(kind='bar')
```

```{.python .input  n=40}
bike_file = "/home/vanboxel/Downloads/pandas-cookbook/data/bikes.csv"
bdata = pd.read_csv(bike_file, sep=';', encoding='latin1', parse_dates=['Date'], dayfirst=True, index_col='Date')
print(bdata[:5])
```

```{.python .input  n=34}
berri_bikes = bdata[['Berri 1']].copy()
```

```{.python .input  n=59}
berri_bikes['weekday'] = berri_bikes.index.weekday
weekday_counts = berri_bikes.groupby('weekday').aggregate(sum)
num_weekdays = berri_bikes['weekday'].value_counts()
weekday_counts['Num Day'] = num_weekdays
weekday_counts.index = ['Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday', 'Sunday']
bpd = weekday_counts['Berri 1'] / weekday_counts['Num Day']
bpd.plot(kind='bar')
```

```{.python .input  n=63}
weather = '/home/vanboxel/Downloads/pandas-cookbook/data/weather_2012.csv'
W = pd.read_csv(weather,index_col='Date/Time')
print(W[:5])
W['Temp (C)'].plot()
```

```{.python .input  n=76}
url_w = 'http://climate.weather.gc.ca/climateData/bulkdata_e.html?format=csv&stationID=5415&Year={year}&Month={month}&timeframe=1&submit=Download+Data'
url = url_w.format(month=3,year=2012)
w_mar12 = pd.read_csv(url, skiprows=16, index_col='Date/Time', parse_dates=True, encoding='latin1')
# Can't actually type the column name, so save it off
tc = w_mar12.columns[5]
w_mar12[tc].plot()

```


```{.python .input  n=81}
# remove degree characters (not sure why it's two chars here, but whatevs)
w_mar12.columns = [s.replace(tc[6:8], '') for s in w_mar12.columns]

```

Remove Columns that have empty (`NaN`) in any rows.  Then drop the redundant
date columns.

```{.python .input  n=85}
# axis=1 is for columns (0 is for rows), 'any' means drop if a col has any NaN (rather than all)
w_mar12 = w_mar12.dropna(axis=1, how='any')
w_mar12 = w_mar12.drop(['Year', 'Month', 'Day', 'Time', 'Data Quality'], axis=1)
```

```{.python .input  n=92}
temps = w_mar12[['Temp (C)']].copy()
temps['Hour'] = w_mar12.index.hour
temps.groupby('Hour').aggregate(np.min).plot()
```


Define a function to get data for the whole year and compare.  We'll remove
columns like we did above.

```{.python .input  n=102}
# I don't know why they wanted to increment the year of the month was one...maybe the API changed?
def dl_month(year, month):
    #if month == 1:
    #    year += 1
    url = url_w.format(year=year, month=month)
    wd = pd.read_csv(url,skiprows=16, index_col='Date/Time', parse_dates=True)
    wd = wd.dropna(axis=1,how='any')
    deg = wd.columns[5][6]
    wd.columns = [s.replace(deg,'') for s in wd.columns]
    wd = wd.drop(['Year', 'Month', 'Day','Time','Data Quality'], axis=1)
    return wd
```

```{.python .input  n=103}
dl_month(2012,1)[:5]
```

```{.python .input  n=124}
w12['Temp (C)'].resample('M', how=np.median).plot(kind='bar')
```

```{.python .input  n=137}
snowiness = snowdays.astype(float).resample('M', how=np.mean)
```

```{.python .input  n=141}
temps = w12['Temp (C)'].resample('M', how=np.mean)
# Name the columns
temps.name = "Temperature"
snowiness.name = "Snowiness"
stats = pd.concat([temps, snowiness], axis=1)
```

```{.python .input  n=142}
stats.plot(kind='bar')
```

Let's compare temp to the dew temp for each month

```{.python .input  n=145}
dews = w12['Dew Point Temp (C)'].resample('M', how=np.mean)
dews.name = "Dew Point"
comp = pd.concat([temps,dews], axis=1)
comp.plot(kind='bar')
```

actually, let's just drop them.

```{.python .input  n=213}
nonzero = requests['Incident Zip'] != '00000'
requests = requests[nonnull & nonzero]
```
